  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

<span id="freeTextContainer6937449420648737885">Everyone thinks they know Libby Strout, the girl once dubbed "America's Fattest Teen."   <span id="freeText6937449420648737885" style="display:none">Everyone thinks they know Libby Strout, the girl once dubbed "America's Fattest Teen." But no one's taken the time to look past her weight to get to know who she really is. Following her mom's death, she's been picking up the pieces in the privacy of her home, dealing with her heartbroken father and her own grief. Now, Libby's ready: for high school, for new friends, for love, and for <i>every possibility life has to offer. In that moment, I know the part I want to play here at MVB High. I want to be the girl who can do anything. </i><br /><br />Everyone thinks they know Jack Masselin, too. Yes, he's got swagger, but he's also mastered the impossible art of giving people what they want, of fitting in. What no one knows is that Jack has a newly acquired secret: he can't recognize faces. Even his own brothers are strangers to him. He's the guy who can re-engineer and rebuild anything, but he can't understand what's going on with the inner workings of his brain. So he tells himself to play it cool: <i>Be charming. Be hilarious. Don't get too close to anyone.</i><br /><br />Until he meets Libby. When the two get tangled up in a cruel high school game—which lands them in group counseling and community service—Libby and Jack are both pissed, and then surprised. Because the more time they spend together, the less alone they feel. <i>Because sometimes when you meet someone, it changes the world, theirs and yours.</i></span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/653920-what-s-the-big-deal-about-prosopagnosia">What&#39;s the big deal about prosopagnosia (the face-blindness)? I have it too (unable to recognize my siblings&#39; faces or even my own) and it&#39;s really not a huge problem. Sure, I sometimes don&#39;t recognize people, but once I explain they usually get it. It&#39;s an annoyance. Broken. Really? Maybe he wasn&#39;t born with it...?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_653920'><a id="like_count_community_question_653920" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/653920?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">22 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28686840-holding-up-the-universe">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/653920-what-s-the-big-deal-about-prosopagnosia">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/653920-what-s-the-big-deal-about-prosopagnosia">See all 19 answers</a>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/32329911-j-toops"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/32329911-j-toops">J. Toops</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Emily, this thread isn't current, but I thought I'd chime in. Prosopagnosia can make life difficult when you combine it with other issues that affe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Emily, this thread isn't current, but I thought I'd chime in. Prosopagnosia can make life difficult when you combine it with other issues that affect social functioning (such as innate introversion). Such as large company meetings, networking if you're in student council or have a job that requires that kind of thing. It is embarrassing at PTA meetings if you're a parent and you've met people for the umpteenth time and they talk to you like they know you and have absolutely no idea what prosopagnosia is (and really don't care to learn). It is scary if you apply it to club/party situations where there is a possibility of assault, but you cannot identify the perpetrator. I've been dealing with this for 45 years, was born with it, and yes, for some people it really is a big deal that affects your family (my husband has been embarrassed and appalled that I couldn't identify him at places), friends (hard to make and retain friends when you can't identify them as they walk towards you at the coffee shop), and employment (most entry-level jobs that aren't data entry are overwhelming and exhausting because you have to recognize repeat customers/clients). After a while, you do feel broken if you do not receive the support and understanding of others around you. "Broken" is a perception, a feeling, that one acquires after negative feedback; sadly, kids and young adults (and adults) are guilty of providing this in bucketfuls.<br /><br />Hope you are enjoying your other reading!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1777658594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1777658594" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1777658594?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1777658594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11838204798088286100"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe no boy will love me or want to touch me ever, even in a dark room, even after an apocalypse when all the skinny girls have been wiped off the earth by some horrible plague. Maybe one day I can be thinner than I am now and have a boyfriend who loves me, but I’ll still be a liar.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I was going to give this book two stars because, honestly, it started well. It was compelling and didn't seem as offensive as the blurb had been, but the more I think about it, the more that doesn't seem to be </span>
  <span id="freeText11838204798088286100" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe no boy will love me or want to touch me ever, even in a dark room, even after an apocalypse when all the skinny girls have been wiped off the earth by some horrible plague. Maybe one day I can be thinner than I am now and have a boyfriend who loves me, but I’ll still be a liar.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I was going to give this book two stars because, honestly, it started well. It was compelling and didn't seem as offensive as the blurb had been, but the more I think about it, the more that doesn't seem to be enough of an excuse for the book as a whole. Yet another book that insensitively <i>uses</i> its characters to create an angsty romance.<br /><br />If anything, I feel more secure in my assessment of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> after reading this book. I got the impression in AtBP that the author was using suicide as a <b>vehicle for romantic angst</b>, and I received a lot of backlash for writing that review. But this just seems to confirm it. I feel like Niven has given very little thought to what it means to portray an obese character and a character with a cognitive disorder. I feel like little thought has been given to any readers who might relate to these characters. I can't help but imagine the author sitting there and simply thinking “how can I make this romance super angsty?"<br /><br />I don't necessarily care that Libby Strout (Libby as in "Lb" and Strout as in "Stout"?!) was called "America's Fattest Teen" or that a major plot point is a game called "Fat Girl Rodeo". These things are gross and offensive, but showing the horrible effects of labels and cruel bullying does not seem like a bad thing to me. No, the bigger problem is that this book actually isn't about bullying, or fat-shaming, or living with mental illness, it's about high school love. That's it. The rest is just window dressing.<br /><br />The author throws together two teens who are <b>solely characterized by their weight and prosopagnosia</b> (the inability to recognize faces) and, despite having zero chemistry, they fall in lurrrve. They are defined by these singular differences - i.e. being the "fat girl" and being unable to recognize anyone, never once feeling like human beings.<br /><br />I'm sure some readers will see the decision to have such different protagonists as an indication of depth, but I truly feel like this is a very shallow book. <b>Stereotypes and cliches abound</b>. Dress it up however you want, but this book is about an unpopular girl who sees herself as unattractive, and a popular good-looking guy who comes to see how said girl is so much better than all those hot, evil cheerleaders he's been dating. His hot, evil girlfriend constantly fat-shames and bullies Libby, obviously, because we all know pretty popular girls are mean, shallow and have no feelings.<br /><br />Also - and this is way more offensive to me than the blurb was - Libby's journey to self-love seems to entirely revolve around finding a guy who will actually like her. I was hoping this would be addressed as the novel wore on, but the small rushed steps toward it at the end were dissatisfying. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Somewhere in this school could be a boy I fall in love with. One of these fine young men might be the one who at long last claims my heart and my body. I’m looking at all the boys going by. It could be that guy or maybe this one."</i>
</blockquote><br />Or she could learn to love herself without a guy? Also, what teenager says "fine young men"?<br /><br />The pacing also slows down as the story moves forward. I remember feeling at one point like the book should be coming to an end, and yet there were almost another hundred pages to go. You knew the characters had feelings for one another, you knew they were going to end up together, but the narrative was dawdling. <br /><br />Then there's my disbelief that Jack has managed to hide face-blindness from his family for years. That seems impossible to me, but I guess this book never was about the reality of the issues it offered up. <br /><br />And, finally, nauseating prose like this:<br /><blockquote><i>The way I feel when I’m with her. Like I just swallowed the sun and it’s shooting out of every pore.</i><br /><br />And Libby's eyes...<br /><br /><i>They are like lying in the grass under the sky on a summer day. You’re blinded by the sun, but you can feel the ground beneath you, so as much as you think you could go flying off, you know you won’t.</i></blockquote><br />There's not a single guy in the world who could tell me I make them feel like they "swallowed the sun and it's shooting out of every pore" without me bursting into hysterical laughter. But, let's be honest, that's the least of this book's problems.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11838204798088286100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1528541705" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528541705" />
    <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys"><img alt="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463498958p2/1053760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528541705?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28671039-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=kick-ass-female">kick-ass-female</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528541705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2506104568302787786">Welcome to the internet in the year 2016. Where a simple book blurb broke the internet for a few days. A teenage girl who was rescued from her house because her weight kept her a prisoner. Then through in a statement about how she is returning to high school aka..the real world after being homeschooled. <br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476139524ra/20806051.gif' alt='commercial photography locations' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I KNOW!! Let's all run and one star and bash the book. <br/><br/>Not. <br/><br/>And all you guys thought I was the biggest bully on here didn't you? <br/><br/>Because I had (for once) stopped to think about what the book </span>
  <span id="freeText2506104568302787786" style="display:none">Welcome to the internet in the year 2016. Where a simple book blurb broke the internet for a few days. A teenage girl who was rescued from her house because her weight kept her a prisoner. Then through in a statement about how she is returning to high school aka..the real world after being homeschooled. <br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476139524ra/20806051.gif" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I KNOW!! Let's all run and one star and bash the book. <br><br>Not. <br><br>And all you guys thought I was the biggest bully on here didn't you? <br><br>Because I had (for once) stopped to think about what the book meant..and it made me drool all over myself.<br>I didn't jump on the bandwagon. I wanted the book even more.<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/california/palm-springs/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453989693ra/17901252.gif" alt="Palm Springs commercial photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Because I've been a bit on the fat side many times in my life. I lose some weight and then I gain some weight. Big dang deal. (I can say that now-I couldn't when I was this character's age.) I home-school my kid. AND YES sometimes we talk about him joining the 'real world' again. Does that mean he is socially awkward? Hell no.<br><br>This book is something that if I had it in high-school I would have highlighted ever stinking line of it. It would have became my Shelby bible of how to deal with all the assholes that dwell in high-school. (and real life)<br><br>These characters:<br>Libby Stout, she is the girl that was taken from her house. By a crane. Because her mom had died suddenly and she could not cope. Food became her crutch, her dad didn't know how to deal with it and tried..he did try. But when someone is bent on self destruction-sometimes that path can't be detoured. She does finally reach that point (when the crane is brought out) that her dad knows that help is needed. He wants to save his daughter. He gets her help.<br>Then comes to the point in the story where she is going back to school. She has lost some weight, she is still overweight by public opinion. BUT this girl totally knows who she is.<br><br>For example..on the first day back at school.<br><b>"Hey," he says.<br>"Hey."<br>"Is it true fat girls give better blow jobs?"<br>"I don't know. I've never gotten a blow job from a fat girl.".</b><br><br>Jack Masselin: This kid hides the fact that he recognizes no one's face. Not even his own family. He once screamed that his mom was kidnapping him because she had gotten a haircut and he didn't have the familiar markers to place her in his mind.<br>He plays the cool guy at school but he lives in fear that someone will discover his secret. <br><br>Then they end up in group counseling together. This is not a boy rescue the fat girl story. This is a story of two people realizing who exactly they are..and owning it.<br><b>People are shitty for a lot of reasons. Sometimes they're just shitty people. Sometimes people have been shitty to them and, even though they don't realize it, they take that shitty upbringing and go out into the world and treat others the same way. Sometimes they're shitty because they're afraid. Sometimes they choose to be shitty to others before others can be shitty to them. So it's like self-defensive shittiness.</b><br><br>Books like this are exactly why I read young adult.<br><br>Jennifer Nevin, I hope you pat yourself on the back. And the haters?<br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476139524ra/20806052.gif" alt="commercial photography locations" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2506104568302787786" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1865903536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1865903536" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1865903536?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=blogging-for-books">blogging-for-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1865903536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4665503819413063432">You know I don't care what anyone thinks, I just loved the hell out of this book! I happy cried so many times in this book. And there will probably be some *SPOILERS* I don't know, my feels right now are out of control. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483834487i/21654650._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This review is going to be all over the place because I'm crazy and that's just the way it is. <br/><br/>I love Libby so much! In this book she has so much courage. Even when she was low and things hurt her, she had courage like no one I know. Those hateful, horrible kids said some of the </span>
  <span id="freeText4665503819413063432" style="display:none">You know I don't care what anyone thinks, I just loved the hell out of this book! I happy cried so many times in this book. And there will probably be some *SPOILERS* I don't know, my feels right now are out of control. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483834487i/21654650._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This review is going to be all over the place because I'm crazy and that's just the way it is. <br><br>I love Libby so much! In this book she has so much courage. Even when she was low and things hurt her, she had courage like no one I know. Those hateful, horrible kids said some of the most horrible things to her. I just can't fathom. <br><br><b>
  <i>My name is Libby Strout. You've probably heard of me. You've probably watched the video of me being rescued from my own house. At last count, 6,345,981 people have watched it, so there's a good chance you're one of them. Three years ago, I was American's Fattest Teen. I weighed 653 pounds at my heaviest, which means I was approximately 500 pounds overweight. I haven't always been fat. The short version of the story is that my mom died and I got fat, but somehow I'm still here. This is no way my father's fault. <br><br>Two months after I was rescued, we moved to a different neighborhood on the other side of town. These days I can leave the house on my own. I've lost 302 pounds. The size of two entire people. I have around 190 left to go, and I'm fine with that. I like who I am. For one thing, I can run now. And ride in the car. And buy clothes at the mall instead of special-ordering them. And I can twirl. Aside from no longer being afraid of organ failure, that may be the best thing about now versus then. <br><br>Tomorrow is my first day of school since fifth grade. My new title will be high school junior, which, let's face it, sounds a lot better than America's Fattest Teen. But it's hard to be anything but TERRIFIED OUT OF MY SKULL. <br><br>I wait for the panic attack to come.</i>
</b><br><br>And of course we all know when she gets to school the jerkholes start bullying her! I hate them so much I could just scream! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483834487i/21654651.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But Libby is a force of nature. She don't take too much shite from anyone! She ignores it or in case of boys, she just knocks them on their arse! She my hero! <br><br>This is the way she meets the other main character, Jack. I love him too. I will get to him in a minute. He's going to do something to Libby that is a horrible prank for the big girls. He puts a note in her bag before talking about it and apologizing, but he gets what he deserves =)<br><br><b>
  <i>I'm lying on the cafeteria floor, and the girl is standing over me. My jaw feels knocked loose, it's over somewhere in Ohio. I give it a rub to make sure it's still attached, and my hand comes away covered in blood. <br><br>I say, "What the hell?" My words are garbled. Jesus, I think she broke my voice box. "Why did you punch me?" <br><br>"WHY DID YOU GRAB ME?"<br><br>My eyes go to her backpack, to the letter sticking out of the pocket I just managed to shove it into. I want to say You'll understand later, but I can't speak because I'm wiping the blood from my mouth.</i>
</b><br><br>Jack is popular dude at the school, but he has a big problem. He has prosopagnosia. <br><br>PROSOPAGNOSIA: 1. An inability to recognize the faces of familiar people, typically as a result of damage to the brain. 2. when everyone is a stranger. <br><br>Jack has figured this out for himself by research. He has never told his family or friends. He gets away with it by other means. You can read the book and find out. <br><br>When Libby was little she lived across the street from three boys and I loved it because she called them Sam, Dean and Cas =) She loved the show "Supernatural" too. They were her only friends, well friends in her head. Until that day she was taken from her home by crane and moved away. <br><br>The story goes back and forth to things that happened in the past to the present. And, it wasn't confusing at all. I'm surprised because I get confused easy! <br><br>It turns out that Libby and Jack are pushed together by being in a group after school for being bad. Then they start to get to know each other and it's so fun and it's so wonderful. They help each other. And yeah, some sad stuff happens but it all works out in the end. <br><br>And let me tell you, there is one part where Libby stands up to the whole school in such a way that I cried my eyes out. I wish I could add the excerpt like the other ones but it's one you should read for yourself. I just love her. Did I say that already? This book makes me feel sad, mad and good. Libby makes me feel good for so many reasons and that's enough for me. I will read this many times and get some inspiration from Libby. I wish I had a friend like her. The saddest part is, I almost didn't read this book because of so many negative reviews. It does have a lot of good reviews but now I don't care what people think, I read what I want and I'm glad. I found a gem that works for ME! ♥<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1470085973ra/19887043.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*I got this print book through the BloggingForBooks Program*<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/01/holding-up-universe-by-jennifer-niven.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br></span>

<div id="review_1834133867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1834133867" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507948675p2/57334157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1834133867?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/57334157-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57334157-caitlin?shelf=2017-read">2017-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1834133867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18374387183048356458"><b>
  <u>
    <i>TIME FOR THE ROAST</i>
  </u>
</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476734148ra/20875062.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I read <i>All the Bright Places</i> last year and ended up dnfing it because I had huge problems with basically every aspect of it. I’m actually really proud of myself for finishing this even though I did skim read the last 25% of it. Honestly, when this book first came out I saw the authors name and instantly avoided this book. However, after seeing a lot of people give it 5 stars – despite all of the problematic aspects I had seen – I decided to pick this book up for the</span>
  <span id="freeText18374387183048356458" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>
    <i>TIME FOR THE ROAST</i>
  </u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1476734148ra/20875062.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I read <i>All the Bright Places</i> last year and ended up dnfing it because I had huge problems with basically every aspect of it. I’m actually really proud of myself for finishing this even though I did skim read the last 25% of it. Honestly, when this book first came out I saw the authors name and instantly avoided this book. However, after seeing a lot of people give it 5 stars – despite all of the problematic aspects I had seen – I decided to pick this book up for the roast.<br><br>Honestly, you can read the blurb and be offended. I sure was. The blurb is a joke, just like the rest of the book. I’m honestly so sick of contemporaries in the present day that are just based around putting 2 characters in the worst possible situation and then forcing them to fall in love – I say forcing because there is 0 chemistry between these characters. I swear some authors just have a big long list of mental illnesses, diseases or unfortunate scenarios that they scroll down and eeny, meeny, miny, moe which ones they will choose. Dead parent for you, random illness for you, a bit of anxiety on the side as well as extreme obesity and we’ve got our perfect story!!!! Everyone will definitely love it!!!!! I strongly question the motives behind writing a novel such as this one.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439225934ra/15810943.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m trying to decide whether I hate Libby or Jack more. I think it must be Libby because dammit she’s annoying as all hell. I actually sent my friends 14 different video rants and then another couple text rants about how annoying this bitch is. In case you forgot <s>I don’t think you could possibly forget because she mentions it every single sentence</s>, Libby was once the World’s Fattest Teen and she’s still obese but she has lost a bit of weight. My main problem with her is that she <b>really</b> does not want to be known as the fat girl anymore but she’s CONSTANTLY talking about it. Her entire inner monologue is just about her weight and omfg it was so infuriating. Also, when she becomes friends with another fat girl she legit says <i>”she talks about her weight a lot.”</i> You’re telling me that this bitch who constantly talks about being fat is complaining that her other fat friend talks about her weight a lot. What on Earth is this bullshit. <br><br>Also, let’s not forget that on her first day of school she walked in and said this to herself:<br><i>
  <b>"Somewhere in this school could be a boy I fall in love with. One of these fine young men might be the one who at long last claims my heart and my body. I am the Pauline Potter of Martin Van Buren High School. I am going to sex the rest of this weight right off me.”</b>
</i><br><br>Let’s also not forget that when she describes her bed, she has to clarify that this is <u>NOT</u> the bed she had when she was trapped in her house because she was so fat:<br><i>
  <b>“I lie on my bed—not the same bed I spent twenty-four hours a day on, back when I couldn’t leave the house, but a new one we bought after I lost some weight."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484009559ra/21671615.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Jack was just a straight up annoying douche and the only thing I liked about this entire book is that he told his little brother that it’s okay if he takes a purse to school because he can do whatever he wants. I appreciate that. I think Jack says it best when he describes himself by saying <i>
  <b>he really looks like an asshole</b>
</i>. I agree, Jack. I agree. But then a few chapters later he says that the song “Sexy Back” is something that should be played when he walks somewhere. For the love of God please shut up Jack. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484009559ra/21671616.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also every other character in this story, like in <i>All the Bright Places</i>, offers absolutely nothing to the storyline and they only add to that awful stereotype that “everyone in high school is an asshole” and “the world is against me because everyone hates me in school”. <br><br>A major problem I have with this authors work in general is that the characters are incredibly one dimensional. Hell, I think it'd be too complex for them to even have a favourite colour - that's how much depth they have. Like in <i>All the Bright Places</i>, these characters are only their physical traits or illnesses and that is extremely harmful. I know that these things can be all consuming but there's a <b>HUGE</b> difference between it being all consuming and it being your entire personality and story.<br><br>If you ignore all of the above problems, this book is still crappy. It’s just a badly written “love story” where 2 characters act like idiots and then “fall in love” despite there being no chemistry. Also, don’t forget that Jack can’t recognise anyone’s face. Ever. BUT DON’T WORRY BECAUSE AT LEAST HE CAN RECOGNISE LIBBY. I mean isn’t that just an amazing loophole. I honestly am not entirely sure if that is a legit thing that could happen. I tried googling it but I couldn’t find anything decent about whether there are actually loopholes. Never forget guys, love can cure everything - including mental illnesses, obesity and MOST IMPORTANTLY RANDOM BRAIN ILLNESSES THAT MAKE YOU FORGET EVERYONES FACE!!!!!!! Just fall in love and you're fixed. <br><br> <b>
  <u>These are not the type of books we need in our lives and I would not recommend this book to anyone.</u>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483622582ra/21631836.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18374387183048356458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1776309984" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1776309984" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1776309984?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1776309984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11496232007211211850"><b>This was equal parts special and frustrating for me.</b> But <i>definitely</i> more emphasis on the special. There were moments when my Vulcan soul FAILED ME COMPLETELY and I turned into a mush of squishy feels. FEEEEEEEELS. I think Jennifer Niven is a WIZARD OF FEELS STABBING and I love her for it. Omg. <b>I did love this book. </b>I did. But there were several things that made me pout in a puddle but I'll get to them in a moment. PATIENCE, GRASSHOPPER.<br/><br/><b>Also: this is not as devastating as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places' title='All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Bright Places</a>.</b> h</span>
  <span id="freeText11496232007211211850" style="display:none"><b>This was equal parts special and frustrating for me.</b> But <i>definitely</i> more emphasis on the special. There were moments when my Vulcan soul FAILED ME COMPLETELY and I turned into a mush of squishy feels. FEEEEEEEELS. I think Jennifer Niven is a WIZARD OF FEELS STABBING and I love her for it. Omg. <b>I did love this book. </b>I did. But there were several things that made me pout in a puddle but I'll get to them in a moment. PATIENCE, GRASSHOPPER.<br /><br /><b>Also: this is not as devastating as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a>.</b> hahhaahha. THANK YOU. I DON'T FEEL LIKE MY HEART JUST GOT RIPPED OUT. But the whole time I was absolutely dreading the ending....so I actually have all the thumping gasping feels anyway because I WAS SO WORRIED. Ahem.<br /><br />I'm having a crisis. Nevermind me.<br /><br /><b>So this story is about being seen, basically.</b> It's equal parts about Libby (who is known as the "fattest teen in America") and Jack (who has prosopagnosia). I reeeally loved the storyline. It was so poignant and beautifully written. Like hold my cupcake, Bob, I need to yell THE WRITING OF JENNIFER NIVEN IS SOMETHING GORGEOUS TO BE UPHELD ACROSS THE MOUNTAINS. I <i>love it</i>. It gets me in the feels and makes me want to do glorious things. I loved the messages of self-worth and I loooved how everything tied together.<br /><br /><b>Brief List Of Other Things I Loved:</b><br />• There are Supernatural references. SO MANY SUPERNATURAL REFERENCES. #win<br />• There is SO MUCH DANCING.<br />• There is much diversity of colour, size, and (briefly) sexuality.<br />• Jack has a gorgeous afro and a deep love of his hair and this pleases me greatly because HAIR APPRECIATION IS MY THING.<br /><br /><b>I love love looooooved Jack.</b> I GOTTA ADMIT HE IS A PRECIOUS CINNAMON ROLL OF BAD DECISIONS. He really makes sucky decisions. And he <i>is</i> a coward a bit. But at the same time I related to him a lot because of the face-blind aspect. I don't have prosopagnosia, but I struggle to recognise people's faces to a mild degree and I fail at reading emotions on faces completely -- so just the fact that Jack could walk into a room of people and have NO IDEA WHO THEY WERE OR WHAT THEY THOUGHT OF HIM was <i>so relatable</i> AND IT NEARLY MADE ME CRY.<br /><br /><b>Libby...I struggled with a lot.</b> This is because she has a very self-righteous attitude and she makes just as many dumb decisions as Jack -- but yet she doesn't seem to ever be sorry about them? At least Jack recognised he was a JERK. Whereas Libby just justified herself. Plus there was a scene at the end <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ where she and Jack had broken up and she was making out with an exchange student until she realised she shouldn't because she still loved Jack....and then she sees Jack kissing another girl and she's got the fury of indignation on her and I just...IS THIS NOT A LITTLE HYPOCRITICAL RIGHT NOW??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But I loved all the self-love Libby talked about and how she had SUCH epic slap-backs to the bullies. Like let me applaud.<br /><br /><b>AND DID I MENTION THERE IS SO MUCH DANCING?!?!?</b> I love it. Jack and Libby just DANCE and it is the most simply beautiful thing of ever. THESE PRECIOUS CHILDREN OF HEART ACHE AND SORROW. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>I also totally got squished with emotions.</b> Mainly <i>"omg this is adorable"</i> and <i>"omg I can't even with how much I love them"</i> and "<i>please do not let my precious adorable cinnamon roll Jack die because I love him so"</i>. Gaahhhhhhhhh...I loved this.<br /><br /><b>I mean, there are a few negatives.</b> Aside from not really connecting with Libby <i>at all</i>, I was surprised that there wasn't much variation in the settings. I didn't really understand a lot of the characters motivations. Like why wouldn't Jack tell his parents he's face-blind?? And why wouldn't Libby go to the principal when she was bullied, yet she told other students to go to the principal when <i>they</i> were bullied?? I IS THE CONFUSED. Also Jack can't recognise his family (fair; he has a disorder and this makes sense) but even in his <i>own home</i> he says stuff like "the man I assume is my father"...which makes no sense, in my opinion, because heck, who else would it be?? I can recognise my family coming down the stairs without even looking at them. Maybe this is just picky: but there was a lot of repetition whenever he was with his family about him figuring out who was who despite it being pretty obvious with faces aside. I mean, he has ONE FEMALE (mother) in his house. Of course it's going to be his mother tell him to put the coffee down or whatnot???<br /><br /><b>All in all: duuuude, this story is a precious little universe and I could not put it down.</b> I COULD NOT!! Every time I did, I wanted to snatch it back up again. I adored Jack and his lion-mane afro and his swagger. And I looove books that want to talk about self-worth and not hiding and just BEING YOU, because these are some of the most important things to talk about of ever. THE WRITING IS DIVINE AND I JUST HAVE SO MANY FEELINGS WHAT IS THIS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11496232007211211850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1841681674" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1841681674" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1841681674?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141357058" href="/book/show/29847082-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1841681674" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer412362296360737502">REREAD! I fell in love with this book allll over again! I adore Libby. I adore what she stands for. I love what this book stands for. The hope it instills. How personal it is to the author and how appreciative I am that she shared her story with us. I'm rooting for this book! I'm rooting for myself. I'm rooting for all the readers who have ever felt less than. As Libby would say about herself, ‘I am magic!’, and so, as are you. <br/><br/><br/><br/><b>Initial review!</b><br/>I'm sure a lot of you will remember the ton of backla</span>
  <span id="freeText412362296360737502" style="display:none">REREAD! I fell in love with this book allll over again! I adore Libby. I adore what she stands for. I love what this book stands for. The hope it instills. How personal it is to the author and how appreciative I am that she shared her story with us. I'm rooting for this book! I'm rooting for myself. I'm rooting for all the readers who have ever felt less than. As Libby would say about herself, ‘I am magic!’, and so, as are you. <br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Initial review!</b><br />I'm sure a lot of you will remember the ton of backlash this book received when the blurb was revealed. I mean, let's not get into that aspect of people having the audacity to judge and write-off a book when they haven't read a single page of it. It's aggravating to the core!<br /><br />So, having read the book, yes, there is a lot of 'fat-shaming' that's mentioned throughout the book. Fat-shaming that the main character has to deal with, i.e. the bullying she goes through, because of her weight. But also the main character 'fat-shaming' herself, because of her insecurity, as a direct result of the bullies and other factors. <br /><br />I personally don't see how this is a problem, to bring to light this sort of issue. Yes, it was slightly uncomfortable to read at times, making it real and raw. But we ask for diverse and complex books/characters, then moan when a 'controversial' topic is raised. This is exactly the kind of realistic bullshit some people unfortunately, have to deal with, as ugly as it may seem. As well as the insecurity and the mental-health issues that come alongside it. I don't understand how it was even assumed that the author was ridiculing people who deal with weight and mental-health problems. If perhaps they'd waited a little longer for some clarification, and did their research, they'd have known that this topic is quite personal to the author. <br /><br />But that's not all that the book is about. Yes, the character struggles with her weight, she's insecure to an extent, but she's absolutely fuckin' strong!!! She's almost sure about who she is. As sure as a teenager can be. She refuses to let her weight define her, stand in her way of her dreams, and fights the fuck back against anyone that dares to ridicule her. And she's happy, dammit! <br /><br />This element is what made the book for me. She was headstrong to begin with, because she made herself be so! Though there are romantic aspects, her problems didn't magically disappear, because there was a guy in her life. But she refused to hide her true self. <br /><br />Because of this, I feel that this book is so empowering! A book that those who feel that can relate to Libby, can find strength in. Though Libby encompasses aspects of her personality that may contradict or clash — i.e. being insecure, yet not giving a flying fuck about anyone — it's a great message that one can take away. You're never fully one or the other, anyway. <br /><br />This is what I personally got from this book. I guess, like every other book, people will interpret it differently, according to their own understanding and worldview. And this is mine. <br /><br /><br /><b> Initial review:</b> <br />Okay, wow. It's 4am. Read this book in less than a day. My heart is floating. I'm dying with feels. <br /><br />I was not expecting to love this book so much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="412362296360737502" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1823347582" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1823347582?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-ya-challenge">2016-ya-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-audios">2016-audios</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1823347582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3233537184768821060"><b> 4 stars!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/HOlding%20UP%20the%20Universe_zpsb7lqcx0h.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480934268i/21365005._SY540_.png' alt=' photo HOlding UP the Universe_zpsb7lqcx0h.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><i>Holding Up the Universe</i> was an interesting and moving read with complex characters and a unique storyline. I listened the the audio version of this book and once I hit play, I didn’t want to stop. When I read <i>All the Bright Places</i> earlier this year, I had the same feeling of being hooked. I’m happy to report the author was able to pull this off not once, but twice. <br/><br/>Our story centers around Libby Strout and Jack Masselin. Libby is formally ‘America’s Fattest Teen’. She’s spent a lot</span>
  <span id="freeText3233537184768821060" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/HOlding%20UP%20the%20Universe_zpsb7lqcx0h.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480934268i/21365005._SY540_.png" alt=" photo HOlding UP the Universe_zpsb7lqcx0h.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Holding Up the Universe</i> was an interesting and moving read with complex characters and a unique storyline. I listened the the audio version of this book and once I hit play, I didn’t want to stop. When I read <i>All the Bright Places</i> earlier this year, I had the same feeling of being hooked. I’m happy to report the author was able to pull this off not once, but twice. <br><br>Our story centers around Libby Strout and Jack Masselin. Libby is formally ‘America’s Fattest Teen’. She’s spent a lot of her young adult life getting healthy and she is nowhere near thin, but she’s happy with herself. She decides to take the plunge, stop homeschooling and go to high school. Libby is a fantastic character. I loved that she’s just herself. She has a great relationship with her dad and meets some good friends throughout this journey for her. She also meets Jack Masselin in a very unconventional way. <br><br>Jack’s got it good in high school, or so everything thinks. He’s popular, has a pretty girlfriend and a lot of friends. He’s funny, charming and cool. But he struggles every single moment of every single day. See, Jack has this secret. He can’t recognize faces. I can’t even imagine how that would feel. To wake up each morning, look at my husband and not recognize his face. That’s how it is for Jack. He knows his brother’s hair style, and he can tell his other brother by his ears, but the system is not flawless. Libby is the only one who knows about this and is able to help him. He doesn't always deserve her help, but that's not the point. It's just the way Libby is. I love her for it. <br><br>Jack and Libby’s relationship is complicated at first. The way they meet, the reason they’re spending so much time together. Their friendship grew and developed as the story progressed. I loved them both and I loved that they had each others backs. Jack won me over early on, just knowing he was rooting for Libby from the very start warmed my heart. Even though there were some hard to read moments, the story, overall, was a positive one. I felt happy when I finished. I give this one 4 stars!<br><i>
  <blockquote>Because sometimes when you meet someone, it changes the world, theirs and yours.</blockquote>
</i><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/HOlding%20UP%20the%20Universe-2_zpsfzwlvi4l.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480934268i/21365006._SY540_.png" alt="Holding Up the Universe photo HOlding UP the Universe-2_zpsfzwlvi4l.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_2164431240" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164431240" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164431240?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164431240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3984839567674292561">ah, yes. so here we are again. the classic case of ‘i can appreciate this book for the story that it is, but it definitely didnt live up to its potential.’ <br/><br/>and i wonder if thats mainly my own fault, and not the books. <i>‘all the bright places’</i> is one my favourite novels ever. its emotionally compelling, lovingly tender, and naturally raw - everything this book is not. so is it fair to judge a different book by the same author when you know they are capable of doing better?<br/><br/>i mean, i really like the</span>
  <span id="freeText3984839567674292561" style="display:none">ah, yes. so here we are again. the classic case of ‘i can appreciate this book for the story that it is, but it definitely didnt live up to its potential.’ <br /><br />and i wonder if thats mainly my own fault, and not the books. <i>‘all the bright places’</i> is one my favourite novels ever. its emotionally compelling, lovingly tender, and naturally raw - everything this book is not. so is it fair to judge a different book by the same author when you know they are capable of doing better?<br /><br />i mean, i really like the idea of the story and how wholesome it could have been - i think diverse representation is something that can always be appreciated. but instead of seeing libby as this strong woman, i saw a whiny brat. and the connection between her and jack didnt feel convincing to me. it was just a lot of superficial high school drama. maybe im getting too old, but i know jennifer niven is capable of writing honest and relatable teen characters, so im not sure why this particular story didnt quite meet the mark for me. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2164431240">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1806325831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1806325831" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1806325831?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141357058" href="/book/show/29847082-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=somebody-s-sick">somebody-s-sick</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806325831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17553712484864237977"><b> <i> “I know what you’re thinking- if you hate it so much and it’s such a burden, just lose the weight, and then that job will go away. But I’m comfortable where I am. I may lose more weight. I may not. But why should what I weigh affect other people? I mean unless I’m sitting on them, who cares?” </i></b> <br/><br/>To be honest, I was not a fan of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places' title='All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Bright Places</a> and I wouldn’t have been this curious about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28686840.Holding_Up_the_Universe' title='Holding Up the Universe by Jennifer Niven' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holding Up the Universe</a> had it not been for the controversy that erupted long before its release. But th</span>
  <span id="freeText17553712484864237977" style="display:none"><b> <i> “I know what you’re thinking- if you hate it so much and it’s such a burden, just lose the weight, and then that job will go away. But I’m comfortable where I am. I may lose more weight. I may not. But why should what I weigh affect other people? I mean unless I’m sitting on them, who cares?” </i></b> <br /><br />To be honest, I was not a fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> and I wouldn’t have been this curious about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28686840.Holding_Up_the_Universe" title="Holding Up the Universe by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">Holding Up the Universe</a> had it not been for the controversy that erupted long before its release. But the more the issue grew, the more I got so pulled to the book that I just had to buy it when it was out on our local bookstores. This time, my gut feel was right and the book is completely worth all my curiosity. <br /><br />Let me help out our community of readers by pointing straight out what the book is/what it is not so as to avoid judging it just by its blurb alone. <br /><br />But before that, just an excerpt from the book about “judging” *winks*: <b>
  <i> “Life is too short to judge others. It is not our job to tell someone what they feel or who they are. Why not spend some time judging yourself? I don’t know you, but I can guarantee you have some issues you can work on. And maybe you’ve got a fit body and a perfect face, but I’ll wager you have insecurities too…” </i>
</b><br /><br /><b> What the book is: </b><br /><br />✔ A contemporary romantic novel so yes, it could be cheesy with several cheesy romantic declarations a girl wouldn’t normally hear from a guy [Now if you don’t like this stuff, then it’s probably not for you. ;)]<br /><br />✔ It’s about mental illness. Both Libby and Jack suffer from unique sorts of mental illness. Libby suffered from depression while Jack has face-blindness or prosopagnosia.<br /><br />✔ A serious read but approached with light, almost comic writing style that addresses social issues with positive conviction and inspiration.<br /><br />✔ A moving, uplifting story that encourages people to be comfortable in their own skin, in their physical appearance/condition because that is what makes every person uniquely beautiful.<br /><br /><b> What the book is not: </b><br /><br />✖ It's not about a fat girl whose life changes because of a cool guy. It’s actually about a cool girl and an equally cool guy who have decided to accept who and what they are even if that isn’t what is generally accepted by society.<br /><br />✖ It’s not about a skinny guy telling the story of a fat girl. It’s about a special guy who sees a special girl not because of her physical weight but of her inner weight, because she has the biggest heart, because she matters greatly. <br /><br />✖ It’s not trying to romanticize mental illness. It’s simply trying to say that everyone should have an equal chance at everything this life has to offer and yes even though it may sound cheesy, that does include love life, romance and all. <br /><br />✖ It’s not against life. In fact, it’s very pro-life. It’s not about just moving on after a loss of a loved one but moving differently, creating new experiences and living life anew. <br /><br />I agree with my friend, (Ate) <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528541705?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelby.</a> (Do check out her awesome, very insightful review by clicking her name). Ms. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/45592.Jennifer_Niven" title="Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer Niven</a> does deserve a pat on the back. If or when I meet her in person, I’m definitely giving her a big, big hug. &lt;3<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17553712484864237977" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2437660495" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437660495" />
    <a title="Fuzaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila"><img alt="Fuzaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532881347p2/55299343.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2437660495?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fuzaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fuzaila" href="/user/show/55299343-fuzaila">Fuzaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=made-me-lol">made-me-lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=romance-lovey-dovey">romance-lovey-dovey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=why-no-hype">why-no-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=really-liked-it">really-liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=50-states-challenge">50-states-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2437660495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1168205568309516429"><b>For everyone who felt that this book is offensive and fat-shaming and trying to garner attention by portraying cognitive disorder - PLEASE KNOW THAT, THIS IS AN #OWNVOICES STORY. JENNIFER NIVEN HERSELF HAD OBESITY ISSUES AND THE PROSOPAGNOSIA PLOT-POINT WAS INSPIRED BY SOMEONE SHE PERSONALLY KNEW. </b> You’d know this if you read the Author’s note. And let’s all give the author space to write about what she wants. Thanks.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453964255i/17896072._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>image source: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525406171?book_show_action=true&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Patty's review</a><br/><br/>Holding Up The Universe is narrated in the point of</span>
  <span id="freeText1168205568309516429" style="display:none"><b>For everyone who felt that this book is offensive and fat-shaming and trying to garner attention by portraying cognitive disorder - PLEASE KNOW THAT, THIS IS AN #OWNVOICES STORY. JENNIFER NIVEN HERSELF HAD OBESITY ISSUES AND THE PROSOPAGNOSIA PLOT-POINT WAS INSPIRED BY SOMEONE SHE PERSONALLY KNEW. </b> You’d know this if you read the Author’s note. And let’s all give the author space to write about what she wants. Thanks.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453964255i/17896072._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>image source: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525406171?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Patty's review</a><br><br>Holding Up The Universe is narrated in the point of view of two teens - Jack Masselin, who has a brain disorder called prosopagnosia which makes him unable to recognize faces, even the faces of his family and loved ones; and Libby Strout, who was once entitled ‘America’s Fattest Teen’. Libby’s lost her mother in an accident and has lost quite some weight since then. But she’s still the fat girl at Martin Van Buren High School. The two become acquainted in detention classes and realize they’re two outcasts with similar problems. <b>Doing full justice to the themes it addresses, THIS IS A BOOK YOU NEED TO READ.</b> Not for the romance, but for the message, for the underlying subject of dealing with obesity and questioning the general norms of beauty in our society. <br><br><b>
  <u>		THE WRITING</u>
</b><br><br>I loved Niven’s writing in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> and I adored it here. Her immaculate consistent flow is very easy to read. BUT. Niven uses these silly similes and metaphors that probably was meant for emphasis, but felt nothing short of ridiculous. <br>Like, see this –<br><br><b> “I feel my stomach drop and land somewhere around the gas pedal.”</b><br><br>Umm, whutt?? Girl, you’re dead then.<br><br>Or this – <br><br><b> “My heart goes hopscotching out of the room and down the hall and out the door and into the street”</b><br><br>Like, WTF?? Just picture that and tell me if you survive.<br><br>And this comes right after –<br><br><b> “And now my heart is nowhere on earth to be found. I can see it as it bypasses the moon and the stars and goes blasting into another galaxy”</b><br><br>Me: *dead*<br><br><u>
  <b>		 MY THOUGHTS</b>
</u><br><blockquote>
<br>•	Fat Girl Rogue is the stupidest game I’ve ever heard of.<br>•	Like, <b>‘hug-a-fat-girl-and-squeeze-the-hell-out-of-her’</b>?? Seriously, WhO cOmES uP WiTh SuCH sHIt??<br>•	Jack’s brother Dusty is a lil’ munchkin I’d like to cuddle.<br>•	Also, <b>DIVERSITY. </b>Jack’s half-black.<br>•	Idk how any kid can live up to 16 years without their parents not recognizing they have prosopagnosia.<br>•	Jack’s parents are either very ignorant or Jack is very potent at hiding his condition from them. UNREALISTIC<br>•	But why would anyone want to hide their prosopagnosia from their parents? <br>•	Wait, <b>Brad Pitt has prosopagnosia?? </b>O.o<br>•	THANK GOD, no insta-love<br>•	And YET<br>•	<b>The Libby-Jack romance was forced. </b>Unrealistic. Unsatisfying. Every other un-insert_suitable_word_here<br>•	If you ask me, <b>the prosopagnosia rep was rather dull. </b><br>•	I still can’t picture how a prosopagnosiac person sees faces. It’s confusing, and may I say, NOT DESCRIBED WELL<br>•	Also did you know, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/89724.We_Have_Always_Lived_in_the_Castle" title="We Have Always Lived in the Castle by Shirley Jackson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Have Always Lived in the Castle</a> is the newest addition to my tbr.<br>•	It makes me effing happy to see characters talking about books and referencing books<br>•	LIKE HECK YEAH, WE’RE BOOK LOVERS WE NEED PEOPLE WHO LOVE BOOKS IN OUR BOOKS<br>•	Libby Strout gives me self-esteem goals.<br>•	And Libby’s dad is THE BEST<br><br><b> “You realize you’ve just asked me if you can skip school and borrow money in the same conversation? You realize I’m the world’s best dad?”</b><br><br>•	AND LIBBY STROUT IN GENERAL IS JUST THE TAKE-NO-SHIT FAT GIRL WITH ANXIETY PROBLEMS YOU NEED IN YOUR LIFE,,,<br><br>•	Look at this – <b><br><br>“I look at Elise’s perfect hair and face and figure. Of course people love to watch her dance. Of course she marries the prince. I wonder what would have happened if Elise had looked like me”.</b><br><br>•	^^This book dwells on everything that’s wrong with the world.<b> Like, look at fairy tales for instance. Every other girl is skinny and fair with perfect blond or black hair and blue/green eyes. No fat princesses, no zits ever on any of those flawless faces. No people of color. Same falls for the Princes too. Except for The Beast who also turns out to be a handsome young prince. I mean, more than half of the population is overweight and non-white but we’ve been raised on these stupid stories filled with stereotypes since the beginning of the world. That you need to look good and ooze beauty for you to have a fairy-tale-happy-ending. hOW THE FRIGGING FRIG DOES THAT WORK??</b><br>•	If you think Libby talks of being fat all the time, think again. That’s what they’re being told Every. Single. Time. They can’t just forget the fact that whenever people look at them they’re being judged for their weight. That’s an accurate rep imo. <b>NOTHING WRONG WITH A FAT GIRL THINKING SHE’S FAT BECAUSE WHAT ELSE IS SHE SUPPOSED TO THINK OF WHEN WE THE PEOPLE DON’T BOTHER TO TELL HER ANYTHING ELSE??</b><br>•	The ending? Nah. I don’t buy that. I wasn’t really invested in the romance, and frankly this book is more than just the romance. It doesn’t dominate the book. It doesn’t dwindle the actual message. </blockquote><br><br>Even with the problematic writing at some places and the unromantic romance, I’d say this book is still a must read. The way it addresses the issue of obesity is what won me over. Of course, it’s nowhere near good as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> and don’t expect it to be heartbreaking either. Just read it! <br><br>Also, remember, DOESN’T MATTER WHETHER YOU’RE FAIR OR DARK, SHORT OR TALL, SKINNY OR FAT, FLAWLESS OR ZITTY, OR JUST ANYWHERE IN BETWEEN - <b> YOU ARE WANTED</b> - <u>DON’T EVER LET ANYONE CONVINCE YOU OTHERWISE.</u> IT’S NOT THEIR PLACE TO JUDGE YOU, NOT YOURS TO JUDGE THEM EITHER. <br><br><br><br>* * * * * * * * * * * *<br><br><b>Initial review -</b><br><br>Forget Leah Burke and every other fat girl, LIBBY STROUT IS WHOM YOU SHOULD BE READING ABOUT</span>
  <a data-text-id="1168205568309516429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
