<div id="review_1527825237" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527825237" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527825237?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28671039-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=gorgeous-covers">gorgeous-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=from-publisher-author">from-publisher-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars">3-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527825237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer547388313892767123">i received an advance copy of this book from the author.<br/><br/>let me begin by saying i wrote my first review of this book nearly 6 months ago. i have been anticipating this book since i finished <i>all the bright places</i> in march of last year. i have been waiting for this copy to show up on my front porch, eagerly, for a month. atbp was one of my favorite reads of last year and the book that got me into reading, the book that fills the first posts of my bookstagram account.<br/><br/>so my expectations were high.<br/><br/>& d</span>
  <span id="freeText547388313892767123" style="display:none">i received an advance copy of this book from the author.<br /><br />let me begin by saying i wrote my first review of this book nearly 6 months ago. i have been anticipating this book since i finished <i>all the bright places</i> in march of last year. i have been waiting for this copy to show up on my front porch, eagerly, for a month. atbp was one of my favorite reads of last year and the book that got me into reading, the book that fills the first posts of my bookstagram account.<br /><br />so my expectations were high.<br /><br />&amp; despite being in a fantasy-only reading slump, i read this in a couple of hours. so that says something.<br /><br />i enjoyed this book. i liked the characters. <b>the face-blindness and weight facets of the book are so important.</b> as with atbp, this book intends to help, which is so good. i can't say i didn't cringe a few times, or have a few WTH moments, but it was so much more artfully done than that first fateful goodreads synopsis--the one that inspired myriad one-star reviews--would have indicated.<br /><br />this book was well-written and unique and so good-hearted. i did not fall in love with this book, but i am in love with the idea of niven as an author. i am so happy that there is a kind soul like her, writing great books and making things lovely. i hope, in a couple of years, to be reading her next!<br /><br /><br /><br />---ORIGINAL JANUARY REVIEW---<br />can everyone please take a chill pill in regards to this book? please?<br /><br />i understand that this is a hot-button topic. i understand that niven's thinness makes this a controversy. i understand that many people were offended by <i>all the bright places</i> (although not nearly as many as the number of people who loved it).<br /><br />but cheese and crackers, people, for a community that reads so much it's kind of bananas how none of you are considering reading the description as a (potentially misguided) attempt at young adult language!<br /><br />the "lifted out of her house by a crane"/other uses of fat as an insult: like i said, probably misguided. but <i>definitely</i> a reflection of the girl's self-image (certainly something that will be a theme throughout the work) rather than an attempt to insult overweight people.<br /><br />"rejoin the human race": oh my gosh, you guys. this is the misreading that really gets me. this is clearly an attempt at imitating quirky-girl diction, NOT A SUGGESTION THAT HER BEING OVERWEIGHT MAKES HER NOT A PERSON. that's ridiculous! that would be so incredibly offensive, and whether you appreciate niven or not you should apply common sense to her wording.<br /><br />and finally, i wish people would stop rating books before they come out and before they've read them. that's not what this is for. this might be a truly beautiful work, and if you don't want to read it you can keep that to yourself. there is no need for you to rate a book one star because you misread its description.<br /><br />thank you for reading this. i hope i didn't offend anyone. have lovely days!</span>
  <a data-text-id="547388313892767123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1703960401">

<div id="review_2012965847" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2012965847" />
    <a title="may ➹" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68157476-may"><img alt="may ➹" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538949856p2/68157476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2012965847?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="may ➹" class="user" itemprop="url" name="may ➹" href="/user/show/68157476-may">may ➹</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-multiple">pov-multiple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=annoying">annoying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68157476-may?shelf=pov-1st">pov-1st</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2012965847" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3883128163683307616">Disappointment and I have become very acquainted over these past few months and I’d just like it to go away for one second so I can go back to blindly loving books again!! <b>I’ve been wanting to read Holding Up the Universe since forever</b>, despite all the pROblemATIc !!! things I heard about it. I thought it genuinely would be a good book and instead… yikes.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>- The main problem with this book is that <b>the characters are developed SOLELY by the things that makes them “different”</b>. </span>
  <span id="freeText3883128163683307616" style="display:none">Disappointment and I have become very acquainted over these past few months and I’d just like it to go away for one second so I can go back to blindly loving books again!! <b>I’ve been wanting to read Holding Up the Universe since forever</b>, despite all the pROblemATIc !!! things I heard about it. I thought it genuinely would be a good book and instead… yikes.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />- The main problem with this book is that <b>the characters are developed SOLELY by the things that makes them “different”</b>. Libby is the fat girl. Jack has prosopagnosia (the inability to recognize faces). That’s literally it. No other traits.<br />- I personally was very meh with all the characters: didn’t love them, didn’t hate them. The only exception is Miss “I’m fat and I don’t want to be thought of the fat girl but I’m going to constantly remind you that I’m fat and that I had to be cut out of my house and I have anxiety and panic attacks but show only a few signs of those and the rest of the time I’m just thinking about how Jack Masselin will sex the weight right off of me” Libby Strout. I guess those could also be her defining features, <b>along with being extremely annoying and irritating</b>???<br />- I also didn’t get the feeling that they were very… human. It was like things literally happened to them and they just let it happen?? There were hardly any times that they felt like actual people with actual emotions and feelings. This was told in FIRST PERSON and yet <b>I felt so disconnected from the characters</b>. Despite being in the characters’ heads.<br />- Basically, it seems like what the author did was add “issues” to the characters and expect them to be fully developed without having to do any actual work herself.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>PLOT</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />- I don’t know what I was expecting, but somehow I was surprised that the whole story was just a <b>high school dramatic love story</b>??<br />- The whole novel is basically <b>one big cliche after another</b>. New girl at school views herself as unattractive and gets bullied. Popular boy with most of the girls at school pining after him suddenly finds something so !! alluring !! about said new girl. And obviously this girl is better than all the mean popular girls that he dated and then they fall in love despite having no chemistry. Forced love, my favorite.<br />- Not to mention that the <b>pretty popular girls are ALWAYS mean</b> and bullying and “used to be better than this but now look at what she’s become”.<br />- Not to mention that ALL girls seek validation from boys—which was shown in this book by both Libby and Jack’s ex (forgot her name)!! <b>That is not an okay message!!</b><br />- It’s like the author thought, I LOVE STEREOTYPES!!!! and decided to stick them all into here to show that high school is that typical time of your life where you’ll get bullied but then fall in love so everything’s okay now!<br />- And that romance. God, that romance. It was SO CRINGY. <b>I swear I lost 5 years of my lifespan</b> each time I came across something like “How does this girl mean so much to me?” or “How could I ever feel anything but lucky that this girl likes me?” <br />- Have a trash bag ready while you read this, not to puke in, but to throw this book in the garbage (where it belongs) when you just can’t handle it anymore.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>MESSAGES</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />- I’ve heard that this book is offensive &amp; problematic, and that it romanticizes mental illness. While I was reading the book, I didn’t see any of that, but after reading reviews about it, I can totally see how this book romanticizes it?? I do feel like the romanticization of mental illness is the “love cures all” mentality, and it didn’t go to that extreme in this book?? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Despite falling in love with Libby and being able to recognize her because of that, his prosopagnosia wasn't COMPLETELY cured. It was just partly cured for her?? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> So yes, it romanticizes mental illness, but like... fully. If that makes sense.<br />- I feel like this book had some pretty good messages about <b>how you’re wanted, no matter your size or shape or appearance or personality</b>. Libby was actually a very strong &amp; independent character sometimes, and I feel like the message she was trying to give was an important one!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>CHARACTERS’ ISSUES</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />- Okay, this was where the weird factor came in.<br />- My <del>utterly horrible</del> BR partner and I were discussing this book and we both agreed that something was just really OFF. But we literally could not name what it was??<br />- We came to the conclusion that <b>the way that the characters’ issues are being portrayed… are not really being portrayed</b>.<br />- YES, it’s about Libby’s fatness. But not really.<br />- YES, it’s about Jack’s face blindness. But not really.<br />- It addresses those issues. But it doesn’t.<br />- It talks about fat-shaming. But it doesn’t.<br />- Like, Libby literally gets hate mail that tells her that she’s disgusting and “how can she eat all that food when people in the world don’t have enough to eat” and <b>she brushes it off as a joke???</b> Maybe it’s that she’s used to it or something, but I’m pretty sure you never get used to hate mail. <br />- Or maybe this is an accurate portrayal of fatness and face blindness? I don’t know. I’ve never personally experienced it.<br />- Again, these issues are literally the only things that define the characters. Like I’ve said before, it feels like the author is using certain issues, slapping them on random characters, and making a love story between them. Yeah, I don’t think I’ve heard of that creative writing course??<br /><br /><blockquote><b><u>DANCE REP</u></b><br /><br />// now I’m just being really picky (also sorry for the really abrupt increase in saltiness, I wrote this part while I was reading the book)</blockquote><br />- If you’re going to include dance in a story, make sure you get the terms right. “Pink ballet toe shoes”—do you mean POINTE shoes? Or pink ballet shoes??? I’m a dancer and I don’t even know what you’re referring too. <b>It really only takes a SIMPLE GOOGLE SEARCH to get it right!!!</b><br />- And then you generalize dance terms by saying “kick” and “bend” and “twist” and “flick” and “shimmy” and “shake” and “boom” and “pop” all over the place. Can someone demonstrate the dance move “boom” to me????<br />- Also???? I don’t see any ballet terms there??? Despite mentioning ballet many times????<br />- And in dance, you don’t TWIRL or SPIN. You TURN. Or PIROUETTE. <b>If Libby is a true dancer like she <i>believes</i> to be, she should know this.</b> Again, it literally takes a simple Google search to figure this out!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <u>PROSE</u>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />- “[...] our eyes are holding hands.” Ummmmmm no eyes can’t hold hands because they don’t HAVE hands???? But thanks for making me imagine a whole arm stretching out from my eyeball!!!<br />- “[...] swallowed the sun and it’s shooting out of every pore.” Yeah what a pleasant image, sounds like Jack levitating off the ground and holding his arms up to the heavens with sunlight pouring out of him like he’s Jesus, but everyone else around him is shielding their eyes because <b>the sight is FRICKING UGLY</b>.<br />- I think that’s enough self-hate for today. Where’s that trash bag again?<br /><br /><br /><br />I’d originally rated this 1.5 stars because I “couldn’t bring myself to care about this book and actually HATE it”, but after I wrote this review and found out that there were barely any positives about this book, I lowered it to 1 star!! <br /><br /><b>This book actually sucks.</b> The characters are so 1-dimensional, everything is so stereotypical, and the book doesn’t ACTUALLY address the characters’ “issues”. It definitely does not do the wonderful art of dance justice, nor does it have writing or romance that won’t make you puke. <br /><br />I mean, if you take out the trash tonight and you see this book resting with all the banana peels and rotten eggs and stale bread, don’t be surprised!!<br /><br /><blockquote>// <b>buddy read</b> with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508-maybelline" rel="nofollow noopener">yam</a></blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="3883128163683307616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10269547780939178444">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>3.5 Stars<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Remember this: YOU ARE WANTED. Big, small, short, pretty, plain, friendly, shy. Don’t let anyone tell you otherwise, not even yourself.<br/><br/>Especially not yourself.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>So this is the super offensive book that no one wanted to read due to a reference in the blurb about how the main character was so fat she had to be removed from her house with a crane. Have none of y’all ever seen My 600 Pound Life???? This wasn’t “fat shaming,” i</span>
  <span id="freeText10269547780939178444" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>3.5 Stars<br><br><b>
  <i>“Remember this: YOU ARE WANTED. Big, small, short, pretty, plain, friendly, shy. Don’t let anyone tell you otherwise, not even yourself.<br><br>Especially not yourself.”</i>
</b><br><br>So this is the super offensive book that no one wanted to read due to a reference in the blurb about how the main character was so fat she had to be removed from her house with a crane. Have none of y’all ever seen My 600 Pound Life???? This wasn’t “fat shaming,” it was spot on accurate. You see, Libby (said craned-out MC) weighed 653 pounds at one point and did, in fact, have to pretty much get the windows blown out of her house in order to be saved when she was almost dying. But instead of people being reasonable, this happened . . . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487878275i/22060500.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And <i>Holding Up The Universe</i> got blacklisted and the blurb had to get changed and a whole bunch of other assholery occurred like the much loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1160020637?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">All The Bright Places</a> magically also became super offensive and apparently now is thought to belittle mental health and oh my Christ now I know why people talk about effing snowflakes so much!<br><br>Read this if you want, don’t read it if you don’t want. I give zero poops. If you decide to give it a shot, kudos to you because you’ll get to meet some interesting people. Not only Libby, but also Libby’s (actually present, which hardly ever happens in YA books) dad, as well as Jack (and everything you never would have known about the disorder prosopagnosia), while you discover sometimes young adult authors write characters who aren’t all white – shocking, I know, and also little brothers like Dusty who decided to start carrying a purse over the summer and believes <b>
  <i>“if I want to carry a purse, I’m going to carry it. I’m not going to not carry it just because they don’t like it.”</i>
</b> You’ll read teens who actually sound like teens and have their share of dickish moments and you’ll get to experience a relatable first crush rather than instalove and laugh out loud when Libby says things like: <b>
  <i>“I want to lean in and get a whiff of him and rest my head on his should or maybe make out with his neck”</i>
</b> while slow dancing with a boy. Or keep being offended just for the sake of being offended, because that seems legit.<br><br><i>ARC provided by Crown Publishing in exchange for an honest review – which took me eleven thousand years to write because I am a jerkoff.</i><br><br><b>ORIGINAL "REVIEW":</b><br><br>THIS book looks offensive? I really just don't understand people. Add me to the OHMYGODGIVEITTOMENOW category please. Because I'm fat, I'm fat and I know it (sh'mon!) . . . <br><br><a href="http://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_2140851191" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140851191" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140851191?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=girl-boy-pov">girl-boy-pov</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140851191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12082659796352253225">Ah, this book... What a sweet love story.<br/><br/>First, the diversity. The heroine, Libby, is fat (though she used to be fatter) and Jack is Black and has a condition that makes him unable to recognize anyone, even friends or the people he loves. <br/><br/>I hope you're not shocked by my blunt description of Libby. If you are, I suggest you do not read this book, because it talks about weight extensively, and Libby is indeed overweight. Although, while this affects her life, she is happy with the fat she lost and</span>
  <span id="freeText12082659796352253225" style="display:none">Ah, this book... What a sweet love story.<br /><br />First, the diversity. The heroine, Libby, is fat (though she used to be fatter) and Jack is Black and has a condition that makes him unable to recognize anyone, even friends or the people he loves. <br /><br />I hope you're not shocked by my blunt description of Libby. If you are, I suggest you do not read this book, because it talks about weight extensively, and Libby is indeed overweight. Although, while this affects her life, she is happy with the fat she lost and is a truly inspiring character who doesn't hesitate to bring up weight in order to make a point. <br /><br />I think many readers didn't like how often weight is brought up in a conversation or how Libby never managed to escape her own, whether at school, in public or with Jack. But as someone who understands what it's like to have more weight than the average girl, I can tell you someone who isn't skinny is faced to think about her weight every single day. It's something you have to accept and start being comfortable with if possible, because there will always be times when you'll wish you could wear that top or for that guy over there to look at you.<br /><br />So you have to kind of be like, YOU KNOW WHAT, I FEEL PRETTY SO SHUT UP. And Libby is the kind of person who'll give you an entire sermon if you start complaining about your weight. She'll motivate you to think differently or maybe even start pulling yourself together and eat and behave in a healthy way. But she herself has to figure some things out. After all, she has been home schooled for many years now, and isn't used to being in public much anymore. So this path she has to take, in order to become familiar again with the outside world, is full of obstacles and little demons, but she knows she has to take it anyway.<br /><br />I know I've barely mentioned Jack--who, incidentally, is a very important character also--but that's because I've connected so much to Libby and she prompted me to think about so many topics. Plus it does somewhat feel like this is Libby's book. Without Jack, some things would be bleak, but there still would be a story. Without Libby, this wouldn't be a book.<br /><br />Not at all a realistic ending though…<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12082659796352253225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1778247784?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778247784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14509769370658327957">I wanted to 'feel' emotions like I did in "All The Bright Places". I was sooooo in the mood for a "All in the Bright Places" repeat-type-experience---that the disappointment that I wasn't going to have my desire filled, only added to my already blue mood I've been in this week. It's not the author fault. <br/><br/>I've read a couple of other books about Prosopagnosia (not having the ability to recognize faces of familiar people). One was a non- fiction book. The other was a fiction- mystery-thriller story</span>
  <span id="freeText14509769370658327957" style="display:none">I wanted to 'feel' emotions like I did in "All The Bright Places". I was sooooo in the mood for a "All in the Bright Places" repeat-type-experience---that the disappointment that I wasn't going to have my desire filled, only added to my already blue mood I've been in this week. It's not the author fault. <br /><br />I've read a couple of other books about Prosopagnosia (not having the ability to recognize faces of familiar people). One was a non- fiction book. The other was a fiction- mystery-thriller story. <br /><br />The structure of alternating narration between the two main characters was simply <br />boring for me.... literally was gonna drive me crazy. <br /><br />My favorite part was BEFORE the story telling really got started---BEFORE the 18 Hours Earlier. <br />Jack begins by saying:<br />"I'm not a shitty person, but I'm about to do a shitty thing. And you will hate me, and some people will hate me, but I'm going to do it anyway to protect you and also myself". <br /><br />I WAS INTERESTED..... when Jack told us he was not a shitty person on the first page......<br />but then, soon, I was bored and didn't care very much about this entire story or the characters. I even found the writing irritating<br />because I got really tired of the characters talking to THEMSELVES ....( on every page - many times on every page). We know that by the type-font change.<br /><br /><br />I'm the last person who should criticize ANYBODY'S writing... because I can't write worth beans! --- which is why I DONT WRITE BOOKS!!!!! -- but between my moody-blue mood - and this 'nails-on-a-chalk-board' tedious predictable style and structure of writing, I wanted to pull my hair out. <br /> <br />2.5.... barely making it into the three star category!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14509769370658327957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1747481105" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1747481105" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1747481105?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1747481105" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12404069508362603207">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars on this one.<br/><br/>Don't go into reading Jennifer Niven's new novel, <b>
  <i>Holding Up the Universe</i>
</b>, thinking this is going to be identical to the phenomenal <b>
  <i>All the Bright Places</i>
</b> (which made my <a href='http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2016/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2015.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>list of the best books I read last year</a>), in tone or the emotional power of its subject matter. I don't say this to denigrate Niven's new book in any way—I think with this book she set out to tell a different and more personal story, yet one with slightly more universal themes.<br/><br/>"You </span>
  <span id="freeText12404069508362603207" style="display:none">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars on this one.<br /><br />Don't go into reading Jennifer Niven's new novel, <b>
  <i>Holding Up the Universe</i>
</b>, thinking this is going to be identical to the phenomenal <b>
  <i>All the Bright Places</i>
</b> (which made my <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2016/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2015.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">list of the best books I read last year</a>), in tone or the emotional power of its subject matter. I don't say this to denigrate Niven's new book in any way—I think with this book she set out to tell a different and more personal story, yet one with slightly more universal themes.<br /><br />"You know how it's easy to believe everything is about you, especially when something goes wrong? <i>Why me? Why do I have the worst luck ever? Why is the universe so mean? Why does everyone hate me?</i> My mom used to say sometimes it's actually about the other person and you just happen to be there. Like sometimes the other person needs to learn a lesson or go through an experience, good or bad, and you're just an accessory in some way, like a supporting actor in whatever their scene happens to be."<br /><br />Libby Strout has already had a brush with notoriety. Once dubbed "America's Fattest Teen," when she weighed 653 pounds at her heaviest and had to be cut out of her childhood home while the media watched, she's spent the last two years being home schooled while she recovered. Now 302 pounds lighter, she's ready to go back to high school and be someone different, someone with tremendous possibilities, new friends, maybe even someone that a guy could fall in love with.<br /><br />When Libby meets Jack Masselin for the first time, it's an encounter that winds up with both of them getting detention, having to go to counseling, and participate in community service for their school. Jack has always seemed like someone who has it all, and knows it—he's good-looking, a bit cocky, and tends to swagger through school. But this bravado hides a significant vulnerability: Jack has prosopagnosia, or the inability to recognize faces, even those of his family members or people he's known all his life. Each time he sees someone, he has to try and figure out who they are, and he's not always successful, which leads to more uncomfortable situations than he'd like.<br /><br />In Jack, Libby sees someone who is hiding their true self, someone who understands what it's like to have secrets and sadness and emotional anguish, while in Libby, Jack sees fearlessness, even when she's being mistreated. But as much as he's drawn to Libby he has to wonder if the persona he needs to maintain in order to protect his secret would ever really give someone like Libby attention. And Libby has to decide whether pursuing everything she wants without worrying about the consequences is actually worthwhile, or if she should just do her best to hide in the background.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Holding Up the Universe</i>
</b> is a story about finding courage when you feel you don't have any, and not letting anyone sway you from what you want. It's also a book about finding hope after loss and difficult times, and how to hang on to that hope in the face of adversity. But more than that, this is a book about letting people see who you really are, and admitting when you need help.<br /><br />There were things I really loved about this book and things that bothered me. I liked some of the characters very much, and loved how Niven revealed their complexities little by little. This certainly was a unique story in many ways, but it didn't feel gimmicky in any way, and there was so much emotion and heart in this story, but it never felt emotionally manipulative.<br /><br />What bothered me is just how cruel Libby's classmates were (even if I know this fact better than I'd like to admit, even all these years later), how unending that cruelty was, and how she really wasn't willing to tell anyone what was going on. There were a lot of things which remained unsaid in this book, and I found that frustrating. I also admit that I wondered whether someone like Jack would actually find himself falling for a girl who still weighed 350 pounds, and that distracted me a little bit.<br /><br />I issued my warning at the start of my review because I'll admit I went in hoping for another <b>
  <i>All the Bright Places</i>
</b>, so some of my disappointment was my own unrealistic expectations. But once I gave it a fair chance, I really enjoyed <b>
  <i>Holding Up the Universe</i>
</b>. It's a book that deserves to be read on its own merit, and although it didn't touch my heart as much as Niven's last book, it still proved Niven's tremendous talent.<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12404069508362603207" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9096574121088904291">just gonna say my opinion, how is the author being offensive towards overweight people? we ALL know overweight people can often be picked on for their size, and if anything the author could just be showing how highschoolers can be horrible and judgemental, and the protagonist is beat down by it, but gets back up and goes back to face old tormentors. which i think is a great way to tell people who deal with bullying that IT CAN GET BETTER, it may take time, but it can happen if you get the right </span>
  <span id="freeText9096574121088904291" style="display:none">just gonna say my opinion, how is the author being offensive towards overweight people? we ALL know overweight people can often be picked on for their size, and if anything the author could just be showing how highschoolers can be horrible and judgemental, and the protagonist is beat down by it, but gets back up and goes back to face old tormentors. which i think is a great way to tell people who deal with bullying that IT CAN GET BETTER, it may take time, but it can happen if you get the right help and are supported. (as for the human race thing, it was never implied that she wasn't human, just that she was ready to go back to school. "human race aka highschool students.") the whole finding someone to make you feel less alone thing could be a problem with this book. but if these 2 students are simply supporting each other, awesome! hopefully jennifer writes their relationship that way and doesn't write it as if all you need is a boyfriend or girlfriend to be happy. if you're offended by the synopsis, that's cool, i can see why since body image is a touchy subject. just try to understand what i'm saying. of course i could be wrong and this book could end up being a fucking mess that is super offensive, but this is just my thoughts on the synopsis. <br /><br />**also there is NOTHING wrong with being "fat" too often it is used in a derogatory way. and i think Jennifer is showing that by mentioning that this girl was bullied because of her body. however the whole crane thing is quite unnecessary (even though it has happened in real life before, and it's how the students see her) <br /><br />*** look at my replies to comments for more elaboration <br /><br />****Prosopagnosia IS A FACIAL RECOGNITION DISORDER, IT VARIES FOR PEOPLE AND PEOPLE WITH IT ACTUALLY USE THINGS SUCH AS BODY SIZE TO KNOW WHO PEOPLE ARE. THE BOY IN THIS STORY IS VERY AWARE OF THE GIRLS BODY SHAPE.</span>

<div id="review_1866713032" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1866713032" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1866713032?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1866713032" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5672774850239761230"><b> 4 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Dear friend, You are not a freak. You are wanted. You are necessary. You are the only you there is. Don’t be afraid to leave the castle. It’s a great big world out there. Love, a fellow reader” </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483832552ra/21654477.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This book shocked me with how much I enjoyed it! Holding Up the Universe is about Libby and Jack. A couple years back Libby had gained so much weight that she needed to be rescued from her house to be saved. Jack has a secret, he cannot recognize faces, not even his own. <br/><br/>The two become conne</span>
  <span id="freeText5672774850239761230" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Dear friend, You are not a freak. You are wanted. You are necessary. You are the only you there is. Don’t be afraid to leave the castle. It’s a great big world out there. Love, a fellow reader” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483832552ra/21654477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book shocked me with how much I enjoyed it! Holding Up the Universe is about Libby and Jack. A couple years back Libby had gained so much weight that she needed to be rescued from her house to be saved. Jack has a secret, he cannot recognize faces, not even his own. <br><br>The two become connected after Jack does something he regrets, and a friendship begins. Through friendship becomes an attraction, but both have personal barriers they need to get past.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458616698i/18508485.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b> <i> “We're all weird and damaged in our own way. You're not the only one.” </i> </b><br><br>I really enjoyed this book, way more than I thought I would. I am not a fan of All the Bright Places, it was one of those books where everyone loved it except me. But I was intrigued by this book and I liked Niven's writing style so I wanted to give it a shot. I myself am overweight, and while I am nowhere near Libby's size I could easily relate to a lot of what she was going through, even though I am an adult. High school is hard enough without adding in the fat shaming factor and I really admired her strength and tenacity when dealing with the hateful comments of others.<br><br>Jack's story was very interesting, I knew little to nothing about face blindness before reading this book. I think Niven did a great job of describing what day to day life would be like living with this condition. Jack himself was one thing I didn't love about this book. He had a lot of growth by the end, but ultimately I still feel Libby deserves a better guy than him.<br><br>Beautifully written, Niven has sold me on anything else YA she writes in the future. I always love when an author has a book I didn't connect with has the ability to write something different, it shows variety in her writing style.<br><br><b> <i> “It's my experience that the people who are most afraid are the ones who hide behind mean and threatening words.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455783307i/18148833._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5672774850239761230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1528586584" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1528586584" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1528586584?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28671039-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone, I guess.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=realism">realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=beautiful-stories">beautiful-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=just-fine">just-fine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=practical-methods">practical-methods</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=positive-ideas">positive-ideas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=preciously-owned">preciously-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=thought-provoking">thought-provoking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=happy-ending">happy-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1528586584" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11559777711169985983"><u>
  <b>***Actual Rating: 3.5/5 Jabby Stars***</b>
</u><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>”I want you to know I’m rooting for you.”</b>
  </blockquote>
</i><br/>It’s interesting that how little time(1~2 days) I spent devouring 84% of the book but I had a hard time(3 days) swallowing the last 16%. Although it’s not entirely a negative sign, it’s indeed something worth discussing about for me.<br/><br/><b>Libby Strout</b> is a girl who never stopped eating for 3 years after her mother died accidentally when she was 10 and she got the reputation of “America’s Fattest Teen” before</span>
  <span id="freeText11559777711169985983" style="display:none"><u>
  <b>***Actual Rating: 3.5/5 Jabby Stars***</b>
</u><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>”I want you to know I’m rooting for you.”</b>
  </blockquote>
</i><br>It’s interesting that how little time(1~2 days) I spent devouring 84% of the book but I had a hard time(3 days) swallowing the last 16%. Although it’s not entirely a negative sign, it’s indeed something worth discussing about for me.<br><br><b>Libby Strout</b> is a girl who never stopped eating for 3 years after her mother died accidentally when she was 10 and she got the reputation of “America’s Fattest Teen” before she was cut out from her house because she was too big to move on her own. <b>Jack Masselin</b> is a boy who has this kind of rare disease called “prosopagnosia,” meaning he can’t recognize faces once they aren’t in front of him and the only way he can be sure about that particular person is by their unique identifiers such as hairstyle, height, body figure, way of walking, or special clothing. <br><br>Even though Libby has lost two-thirds of her weight, she’s still the one occupying the largest space in a high school classroom. Thus, as stereotypical as those students could be, they noticed her in her first day of school after she locked herself up in the bedroom, lying on the bed, doing nothing but reading and eating for years. <blockquote>
  <i>”Here’s the worst thing of it,” I say. “You know how far I’ve come and I know how far I’ve come, <b>but everyone else just sees me for how large I am or where I was years ago, not who I am now.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br>Her classmates, including Jack and his idiot friends, begin to make fun of her, speak ill of her, spread rumors of her and bully her. But that’s also how Libby meets Jack. In a stupid prank called “Fat Girl Rodeo,” Jack is challenged to grab their so-called “grand prize,” aka Libby and hold on to her like a life string. To show he’s not a coward, he accepts the challenge reluctantly and is rewarded by a punch in the mouth from her.<br><br>The only thing I find heartwarming is the fact that Jack has rooted for her since the day she was cut out from her bedroom and carried by a crane. He didn’t humiliate her as others did and he truly saw her as a person, a nice and funny and trust-worthy person. Even after all those years, he still doesn’t waver. <br><blockquote>But then I see her. <i>Libby Strout.</i> She’s lowered from the ceiling by a crane, larger than life, larger than anyone, and <b>she’s the only one with a face.</b>
</blockquote><br>By the way, that’s why I chose <i>”I want you to know I’m rooting for you.”</i> to be my most favorite slogan for the book!<br>Therefore, their romance here is probably the purest type I’ve ever seen and I honestly like it. I can see that whenever they talk, they’re living in their private bubble and nobody in the world can interrupt their conversation nor can anyone deprive them of their borrowed freedom. <br><blockquote>
  <i>”But after I danced you to the door, I’d want to kiss you.”<br>“You would?”<br>“I would.”<br><b>And now my heart is nowhere on earth to be found. I can see it as it bypasses the moon and the stars and goes blasting into another galaxy.</b><br>“Hypothetically.”<br>“Well then, I would let you kiss me.”<br>“Hypothetically?”<br>“<b>No. Definitely.</b>”<br>By the time we hang up two hours later, it’s 1:46 a.m. I lie there for the rest of the night waiting for my heart to return to my chest.</i>
</blockquote><br>To my disappointment, I actually don’t find the main point of the story (and it’s also how <b>”You are wanted.”</b> becomes the most notable quote)—when Libby wears her purple bikini and hands out sheets of flier in public that says “YOU ARE WANTED” along with her personal story—memorable or meaningful. I mean, she’s proving to everyone that she isn’t that girl who scarfed all the junk food down her throat nonstop and gave up on herself but instead, she’s already stepped out of her comfort zone and decided to blend into the rest of them. However, I can’t connect to her at all by the means she uses so the whole scene looks a bit out of place for me. <br><br>Aside from Libby, there’s also something about Jack that’s been bugging me since I first started reading the book. The fact that Jack was <b>the only person</b> who knows what happened to his brain and that he can’t tell who is who when too many faces are flashing before his eyes until he told Libby doesn’t make much sense to me. Not that I’m always trying to look for evidence or something, it’s just that I’ll be more appreciative if the authors write a story based on something specific and reliable. What I can’t understand is <i>how come Jack’s parents or brothers didn’t know something’s wrong with his behavior?</i> What I’m saying is that it’s not easy to go unnoticed when you suffer from some sort of <i>neurological disorder</i> for more than 10 years! <br><br>Mercifully, Jennifer ended the story in a really positive and uplifting way. As usual, I feel powerful and energetic after finishing the book because she made Jack and Libby a happy couple and wrapped all those matters up lovely. Besides, there’s a part I absolutely love and it’s when Libby leaves her favorite book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/89724.We_Have_Always_Lived_in_the_Castle" title="We Have Always Lived in the Castle by Shirley Jackson" rel="nofollow noopener">We Have Always Lived in the Castle</a>, on a bench in the park for someone—anyone—to pick it up. I guess it’s actually from one of Jennifer’s interviews videos on YouTube, where she “dropped” some of her favorite books randomly on the streets, near the telephone booth, or beside a statue in London. If you’re interested, you could watch it <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SEyG0eVz07M" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!<br><br>Again, it’s amazing to finish another inspirational book from Jennifer Niven. Despite the fact that I don't love it (but I LIKE it), I’ll still recommend it to everyone. After all, there’s definitely something worth learning and hearing from the protagonists. <b>To those who haven’t read any of Jennifer’s books, I highly suggest you start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> because that one is by far the best book I’ve read in my life.</b> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477218593i/20928809._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11559777711169985983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1953226645">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1529393109" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529393109" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529393109?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28671039-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=false-advertising">false-advertising</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=psychological">psychological</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=multi-povs">multi-povs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529393109" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10600182289672576306"><b>Initial reaction reading this book:</b> I don't know if I'm angry at this book as much as I am just completely left exhausted and drained by this book, and not even in a fulfilling way. (I mean, I've been left completely gutted by Courtney Summers and Lauren Oliver's narratives before, but in ways that made me feel like I identified with the weight of the character's struggles and situations, and to me, the characters they crafted were dimensional, well-thought out, and kept me reading to see what w</span>
  <span id="freeText10600182289672576306" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction reading this book:</b> I don't know if I'm angry at this book as much as I am just completely left exhausted and drained by this book, and not even in a fulfilling way. (I mean, I've been left completely gutted by Courtney Summers and Lauren Oliver's narratives before, but in ways that made me feel like I identified with the weight of the character's struggles and situations, and to me, the characters they crafted were dimensional, well-thought out, and kept me reading to see what would become of the characters.<br><br>I think the problem I have with Niven's narrative here (and I had this same problem with "All the Bright Places") is that her characters are too singular in dimension to me, and the problems expounded upon are things that not only lack a certain connectivity despite being well researched and getting some things right in terms of the emotional roughness, but it doesn't feel REAL. It doesn't feel GENUINE. It feels like the characters are a means to an end for the purposes of creating a relationship and isolating their differences so that they are SOLELY DEFINED by those differences (despite claims to the otherwise). And the horrible sluggish pacing in this book just amplified that even more because it felt like certain points were rehashed and told instead of shown. <br><br><b>Full review:</b><br><br>I'll try to keep my reaction short and sweet for this book, but in sum: I didn't care for it for a number of reasons. I was willing to pick this book up despite my experiences with "All The Bright Places" (which I didn't care for either, but I did applaud some aspects of the novel in the aftermath of the overarching read).<br><br>Having picked up "Holding Up the Universe" revealed some of the same issues that bothered me in "All The Bright Places", but there were other issues that surprised me that were unique to this book. Again, I applaud the fact that Jennifer Niven chose to write about two teens with unique and horrifying experiences based on the prejudices of people who don't understand them and the fear associated with being continuously stigmatized and misunderstood (at least taking the intentional bare bones of this story for what they are). I applaud that she shows how the two teens with these unique experiences come together in a relationship of some form (again: bare bones intention of the narrative).<br><br><b>Problem is that the execution of this narrative for those intentions was not done well.</b><br><br><b>Problem #1:</b> <i>Poor pacing. </i> I think this was the biggest achilles heel of the overarching work and I think that ruined it for me on one level. Reading the narrative felt like a rambled slog at times (though I don't fault the audiobook narrators who read this book - they were good). There's a good reason why a good rule of thumb for writing is SHOW don't TELL. This book told too many experiences of the characters and tried to explain them to the point where segments of the narrative felt repeated more for theme than they should've been. There were some moments where the narrative got it right as per Libby's struggles with public perception, bullying, and rationalization to her weight loss, but it felt too dictated to me. Also with respect to Jack's condition, he's struggling to make sense of it and come to terms with it, but I also felt like there were sections of the narrative that weren't paced well and repetitious to his experiences to where it kept throwing me out of the narrative despite his emotional upheavals and conflicts.<br><br><b>Problem #2:</b> <i>Characters being used as a means to an end.</i> Let's just admit something off the bat: THIS IS A ROMANCE. And there's nothing wrong with that, I knew that coming in and was fine with that. But when you craft a narrative where the sole purpose of the overarching story is to bring two characters who are labeled by the world as "freaks" (and this was done in "All the Bright Places" to the point where I was like "Seriously?") to fall in love with each other and it's so blatantly obvious even if the characters have next to no chemistry and are "instaplaced" with each other - there's your problem right there. It's not only emotionally manipulative, it's really being reductive in terms of the personal pains and struggles that they're going through. It also reduces them to a "condition" rather than being more dimensional human beings. I hated that feeling in the narrative. I sincerely felt unconvinced of the relationship between Libby and Jack, even long after I finished the last page of the book. My mind kept tuning out because the narrative kept trying to "explain" this chemistry. I didn't like that at all.<br><br><b>Problem #3:</b> Reducing characters solely to a "condition" or "status": This ties in with the last point. You know, I applaud anyone who will tackle what it's like to live as something that isn't fitting the majority or status quo or able body norm and presents unique challenges for the people whose stories are being told in a narrative, but you have to be careful that you don't shape the character's experiences solely by those terms. People (even those in stories) are more dimensional and complex than that. Yes, those experiences are essential to the person's life and identity, but they are not the sole definition points you should be using to shape that identity. Sure, exploring the challenges of attitudes that may be put to the person with that condition, and also exploring the fears, doubts, that person may have with that experience is essential and necessary, but you have to be careful about exploring it, because it can easily become a point where you become reductive in detailing that person's experience(s). <br><br>It would be like someone telling me "Oh, you suffered from epilepsy/seizures for the first eight years of your life, that makes you a freak, so the only person who could ever love or understand you is someone who is just as socially ostracized as you are, and there's no one you can talk about it to, and it's going to keep you messing up in life and you're just going to be miserable until you find love in someone else, because apparently your self-love doesn't exist unless you're with that person ." (To which I would say a firm screw that noise. Also: true story.)<br><br>*sighs* I feel like Niven sends mixed messages (again) in the narrative, this time about body image and a rare brain disorder, as opposed to her previous narrative with bipolar disorder and the survivor's guilt of another character. And while the narrative does explore backgrounds as to how they both came to be, it still feels like a means to an end which lends me to say it doesn't feel REAL or GENUINE.<br><br>If someone asked me whether this book was a good example of showing body positivism I would say a firm goodness no. Yes, it does show the prejudice and ostracism and isolation and self-loathing/fear the characters feel, but I don't feel like the narrative does a good job with actually DEALING with the complexity of those experiences and why they are, where they come from without dictation. Only towards the end of the narrative do the characters have something of a coming to terms and it's a quick resolution that feels unfulfilling and lacking the weight of the events that led up to that ending.<br><br>So...in sum, not my cuppa. And it saddens me to say that, yet again, I've had this experience with Niven's work. Maybe I'll have better luck in another work, I guess, but I'm not so confident, unfortunately.<br><br>Overall score: 2/5 stars.<br><br>Edit: 2/5/2016 I'm glad the synopsis (Finally!) changed, though some issues still remain to be seen with how the story chooses to handle these subjects. We'll see.<br><br><b>Initial reflection:</b><br><br>Definitely not here for the horrible, weight shaming premise noted for this book on GR (I'm speaking as a woman who's struggled with weight issues most of my life, but yet I've worked with overweight kids/teens in the past in my educational field of sports medicine.)<br><br>That said, I'm probably going to end up reading this book. And I won't be too happy if it completely botches the topic.<br><br>If people are interested in reading about overweight teens as protagonists, here are a few for reference, though some of them I haven't read yet:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2698889.Artichoke_s_Heart" title="Artichoke's Heart by Suzanne Supplee" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1407895916s/2698889.jpg" alt="Artichoke's Heart by Suzanne Supplee" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/253106.The_Earth__My_Butt__and_Other_Big_Round_Things" title="The Earth, My Butt, and Other Big Round Things by Carolyn Mackler" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1405148355s/253106.jpg" alt="The Earth, My Butt, and Other Big Round Things by Carolyn Mackler" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6931356.The_DUFF_Designated_Ugly_Fat_Friend" title="The DUFF Designated Ugly Fat Friend by Kody Keplinger" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1271108843s/6931356.jpg" alt="The DUFF Designated Ugly Fat Friend by Kody Keplinger" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18304322.Dumplin___Dumplin____1_" title="Dumplin' (Dumplin', #1) by Julie Murphy" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1424189465s/18304322.jpg" alt="Dumplin' (Dumplin', #1) by Julie Murphy" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15798674.Fat_Angie" title="Fat Angie by E.E. Charlton-Trujillo" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1351213550s/15798674.jpg" alt="Fat Angie by E.E. Charlton-Trujillo" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1114929.Big_Fat_Manifesto" title="Big Fat Manifesto by Susan Vaught" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1317064236s/1114929.jpg" alt="Big Fat Manifesto by Susan Vaught" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3695909.Everything_Beautiful" title="Everything Beautiful by Simmone Howell" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1312058762s/3695909.jpg" alt="Everything Beautiful by Simmone Howell" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/91817.Name_Me_Nobody" title="Name Me Nobody by Lois-Ann Yamanaka" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1171235530s/91817.jpg" alt="Name Me Nobody by Lois-Ann Yamanaka" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Edit: To give some context on how offensive this book blurb is:<br><br>I've experienced bullying over my weight when I was a kid and I've also heard/read stories from kids/teens/adults who've experienced the same in my field of expertise. The fact that the blurb points out that she had to be lifted out of the house via a "crane" isn't amusing or funny, it's horrifying, even if it's intended to be a snarky remark. And the fact that she's supposedly "[rejoining] the human race" is shaming the girl for her weight because it's implying that she's lazy or a sloth or to blame somehow for her size - it diminishes her worth as a person. It plays into the bullying and belittling dialogues about people who are overweight rather than allowing people to love themselves for who they are, no matter their weight.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10600182289672576306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer14205667711106726392">From the description, it sounded like <i>All the Bright Places</i> meets <i>Bone Gap</i> -- which sign me the fuck up!<br/><br/>But in practice, I couldn't get past the first 10%. It seemed like Jennifer Niven spent the whole time trying to convince me these characters were interesting, rather than them actually being interesting. It wasn't that the story was bad, it's just that--after reading <i>All the Bright Places</i>--I have such high regard of Jennifer Niven that I didn't want this to ruin it.<br/><br/>Think I'll try <i>Velva Jean L</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14205667711106726392" style="display:none">From the description, it sounded like <i>All the Bright Places</i> meets <i>Bone Gap</i> -- which sign me the fuck up!<br /><br />But in practice, I couldn't get past the first 10%. It seemed like Jennifer Niven spent the whole time trying to convince me these characters were interesting, rather than them actually being interesting. It wasn't that the story was bad, it's just that--after reading <i>All the Bright Places</i>--I have such high regard of Jennifer Niven that I didn't want this to ruin it.<br /><br />Think I'll try <i>Velva Jean Learns to Drive</i> instead.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28671039-holding-up-the-universe">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359586-stacee?shelf=doctor-who-reference">doctor-who-reference</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359586-stacee?shelf=present-and-positive-parents">present-and-positive-parents</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7359586-stacee?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1526296178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4735373917478221027">This was just as amazing as I was expecting it to be. <br/><br/>Jack and Libby are fantastic characters who took me on a roller coaster of feels. I was gleeful, swooning, heartbroken, and cheering. There are positive and present parents {which I always delight in seeing} and one little brother I wanted to squeeze. <br/><br/>Yes, there are some horrible moments. Yes, there is bullying. Yes, there were some characters that I wanted to jump into the book and make them walk barefoot on Legos. But, there is growth. Ther</span>
  <span id="freeText4735373917478221027" style="display:none">This was just as amazing as I was expecting it to be. <br /><br />Jack and Libby are fantastic characters who took me on a roller coaster of feels. I was gleeful, swooning, heartbroken, and cheering. There are positive and present parents {which I always delight in seeing} and one little brother I wanted to squeeze. <br /><br />Yes, there are some horrible moments. Yes, there is bullying. Yes, there were some characters that I wanted to jump into the book and make them walk barefoot on Legos. But, there is growth. There is acceptance. And there is a wonderful declaration that everyone needs to read. <br /><br />It might be easier to say that I loved every bit of it. <br /><br />**Massive thanks to Random House for sending me a bound manuscript and making me scream in the post office when I saw it**</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ofDsWPKMkXS4VTb07CZokBcw/LDhYCecEIr4r1sO7tab1oWKSdJYHB9+gpUb02JPwW8beC/tqftL9L4elk0cTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1272645494061144162">Jennifer Niven is the Emmy Award-winning #1 New York Times and International bestselling author of ten books, including All the Bright Places and Holding up the Universe. Her books have been translated in over 75 languages, and All the Bright Places has won literary awards around the world, including the GoodReads Choice Award for Best Young Adult Fiction of 2015. It was named a Best Book of the Y</span>
  <span id="freeText1272645494061144162" style="display:none">Jennifer Niven is the Emmy Award-winning #1 New York Times and International bestselling author of ten books, including All the Bright Places and Holding up the Universe. Her books have been translated in over 75 languages, and All the Bright Places has won literary awards around the world, including the GoodReads Choice Award for Best Young Adult Fiction of 2015. It was named a Best Book of the Year by Time Magazine, NPR, the Guardian, Publisher's Weekly, YALSA, Barnes &amp; Noble, BuzzFeed, the New York Public Library, and others, and was the #1 Kids' Indie Next Book for Winter '14-'15. The film starring Elle Fanning, Justice Smith, Luke Wilson, and Keegan-Michael Key, is now streaming on Netflix, with a script by Jennifer and Liz Hannah (The Post). <br /><br />Jennifer is currently at work on her fourth and fifth novels for young adults, with number three— Breathless— coming out September 29. She also oversees Germ, a literary and lifestyle web magazine for girls and boys age high school and beyond that celebrates beginnings, futures, and all the amazing and agonizing moments in between. Her previous works include four novels for adults, as well as three nonfiction books. She divides her time between Los Angeles and coastal Georgia with her husband, kids, and literary cats. </span>
